(**philosophical track / distributional lineage**)
- [`base/sources/armendariz-2020-cosimlex.md`](base/sources/armendariz-2020-cosimlex.md) — Armendariz, Purver, Ulčar, Pollak, Ljubešić & Granroth-Wilding 2020, LREC (arXiv 1912.05320), "CoSimLex: A Resource for Evaluating Graded Word Similarity in Context"; a resource paper describing **graded human ratings of word-pair similarity in two contexts** (0-to-6 scale; 27 EN MTurk annotators, 12 each for HR/FI/SL; built on SimLex-999; the gold standard for **SemEval-2020 Task 3, GWSC** — a distinct shared task). The **Option-B graded-anchor alternative to DWUG** that [`decisions/resolved/lexical-sense-gradience-anchor`](decisions/resolved/lexical-sense-gradience-anchor.md) flagged — but its unit is **different-word pairs across contexts**, not DWUG's same-lemma usage pairs, so it does **not** fit the monotonicity clause out of the box (consistent with DWUG's own "Fit assessment"). Primary-verified two facts the [`resource/dwug-usage-graphs`](base/resources/dwug-usage-graphs.md) page had only secondarily: scale = **0 to 6** (not "0–10"), and that Zenodo record 3989788 is the **distinct SemEval-Task-3 artifact** (the CoSimLex paper itself states no license/URL) — both corrected on the DWUG page this session. **`source` page, NOT yet an anchor** (license + fetchability + released counts must be firsthand-verified before any anchor use). **status: received** (abstract + 9 §-located body quotes verbatim-verified against the ar5iv rendering of arXiv 1912.05320 + ACL Anthology metadata, 2026-06-24). (**philosophical track / lexical line**)
- [`base/sources/cruse-1986-lexical-semantics.md`](base/sources/cruse-1986-lexical-semantics.md) — Cruse 1986, *Lexical Semantics* (Cambridge); the standard textbook of the **descriptive sense-relation tradition** — the **lexical unit** (form + a single sense), the **systematic sense relations** (hyponymy/meronymy/antonymy/troponymy), and above all the **selection vs. modulation** distinction: context either *selects* a discrete sense (→ ambiguity) or *modulates* within a single sense by highlighting/backgrounding traits (→ generality, "not discrete but continuous and fluid"). Fills the "pending Cruse" gap [`concept/polysemy`](base/concepts/polysemy.md) named in its Honest-gaps section. Note the page is careful that Cruse's selection/modulation is the *within-sense-vs-between-senses* axis (generality vs. ambiguity), **not** the project's *relatedness-between-senses* gradient (discrete-but-related senses are *selection*, not modulation) — Cruse contributes *convergent* motivation (he reportedly dislikes the polysemy/homonymy terms and prefers "discrete vs. continuous semantic variability"), not an identity. Cruse's "contextual normality as the main mechanism for sense selection" is the **lexical-semantics statement of the project's distributional null**. **SECONDARY-ONLY / primary UNREACHABLE as OA** (in-copyright Cambridge monograph; full-text hits are unauthorized mirrors, excluded by policy as for Goldberg/Croft/Firth): one direct Cruse quote (the "basic problem" line) via **Kilgarriff 1997** (no page), the modulation/selection exposition via the in-repo **CoSimLex** page (Armendáriz et al. 2020), the lexical-relation definition via **Mohammad & Hirst 2012** — every claim flagged "primary NOT consulted"; only one page locator (autohyponymy pp. 63–65, Kilgarriff's, **unverified**). **Theory/descriptive source, NOT a human anchor** (grounds vocabulary the project's lexical wedge uses, never a model result; the graded human anchor stays Usim/DWUG/CoSimLex-class data). `refines` [`concept/polysemy`](base/concepts/polysemy.md); `depends-on` [`source/armendariz-2020-cosimlex`](base/sources/armendariz-2020-cosimlex.md). **status: received** (secondary-strength, 2026-06-26, session 120). (**philosophical track / lexical line**)
- [`base/sources/fillmore-1982-frame-semantics.md`](base/sources/fillmore-1982-frame-semantics.md) — Fillmore 1982, "Frame Semantics" (in *Linguistics in the Morning Calm*, Hanshin, Seoul); the paper that names **frame semantics** — a word's meaning is understood only against a structured background *frame* of related concepts it evokes — the theory tying the lexical and grammatical levels (words, idioms, constructions all form-and-frame pairings) and the direct ancestor of Construction Grammar and FrameNet. A knowledge-frame counterweight to the purely `distributional` founding sources: Fillmore's "company" is a structured frame, not a co-occurrence neighborhood. **Primary UNREACHABLE as open access**: a **partly-thin, secondary-and-preview page** — two opening sentences read firsthand only via a registration-walled 2006-reprint preview (pagination from p. 373, NOT the 1982 original), the "By the term 'frame'…" definition carried via metaphorhacker.net (2014) with no locator; **no 1982-original page number asserted as read**. **Theory source, not a human anchor** (grounds a theory a model may instantiate, never a model result). **status: secondary-only** (deliberate non-standard status string — primary not consulted; logged 2026-06-24). `refines` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md); `depends-on` [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md). (**philosophical track / constructional line**)
- [`base/sources/goldberg-1995-constructions.md`](base/sources/goldberg-1995-constructions.md) — Goldberg 1995, *Constructions: A Construction Grammar Approach to Argument Structure* (Chicago UP); the **founding book-length statement of Cognitive Construction Grammar** — the basic unit of grammar is the **construction**, a form–meaning pair "not strictly predictable from C's component parts" (definition attributed p. 4), and argument-structure patterns (ditransitive, caused-motion, *way*-construction) carry meaning independently of their verbs. The charter-core primary for the project's caused-motion / way-construction / coercion lines; upgrades the "Goldberg 1995; not in-repo" flag in [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md) and [`concept/coercion`](base/concepts/coercion.md) to a sourced (secondary-attributed) provenance, and attaches Boas-attributed stimulus locators (caused-motion examples p. 152, way-construction pp. 199–218). **Primary UNREACHABLE as open access**: a **thin, secondary-only page** — the in-print Chicago book has no OA full text or readable preview (publisher catalogue only; Google-Books preview JS-walled, served no body text; Princeton self-archive routes all HTTP 403). **Every quote is carried via fetched named scholarly secondaries** (two Hans C. Boas CxG chapters quoting Goldberg 1995 verbatim with locators; one CxG preprint for framing; one excerpt-notes page for the p. 1 thesis), each flagged; **no 1995-original page number asserted as read**. **Theory source, not a human anchor** (grounds a theory a model may instantiate, never a model result). **status: secondary-only** (deliberate non-standard status string — primary not consulted; logged 2026-06-25). `refines` [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md) + [`concept/coercion`](base/concepts/coercion.md); `depends-on` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md). (**philosophical track / constructional line**)
- [`base/sources/goldberg-2006-constructions-at-work.md`](base/sources/goldberg-2006-constructions-at-work.md) — Goldberg 2006, *Constructions at Work: The Nature of Generalization in Language* (OUP); the **usage-based extension** of Cognitive Construction Grammar and the sequel to the 1995 founding statement. Turns from "constructions carry meaning" to the **nature of generalization**: how constructional generalizations are learned from finite input and **constrained** against overgeneralization — its two signature mechanisms **statistical preemption** (indirect negative evidence: repeatedly hearing a competing pattern lets the learner infer the other is not conventional) and a pattern's **degree of openness / type frequency**. Broadens the 1995 "iff" construction definition to admit *fully predictable but sufficiently frequent* patterns (the usage-based "+ frequency" clause), and is explicitly **usage-based** (frequencies + fully-compositional individual patterns stored *alongside* generalizations) — the natural hinge from the `constructional` wedge toward the `distributional` tag. **2006 book body UNREACHABLE as open access** (Google-Books preview-walled / blurb only; OUP catalogue metadata-only; archive.org borrow-only controlled-lending; SIL review 403) — **but quotes carried via Goldberg's own self-archived 2009 *Cognitive Linguistics* précis** ("The nature of generalization in language," 20(1):93–127, DOI 10.1515/COGL.2009.005; fetched + text-extracted), **author-primary** text (stronger than the 1995 Boas-secondary chain) though a précis restatement, not the book's pages; the **only** book-page locator is the définition "(Goldberg 2006:5)" as Goldberg reproduces it. **Theory source, not a human anchor.** **status: secondary-only** (book body unread; logged 2026-06-25, session 108). `refines` [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md); `depends-on` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md). (**philosophical track / constructional line**)
- [`base/sources/croft-2001-radical-construction-grammar.md`](base/sources/croft-2001-radical-construction-grammar.md) — Croft 2001, *Radical Construction Grammar: Syntactic Theory in Typological Perspective* (OUP); the **typological, non-reductionist wing** of Construction Grammar. Pushes the constructionist commitment to its strongest form via **linguistic typology**: (a) **constructions as wholes are the primitive units** of syntax; (b) **syntactic categories (Noun, Verb, Subject, Object) are not universal building blocks** but are *derived from* constructions — defined by their **distribution** in construction roles, hence **language-specific and construction-specific**; (c) a **cross-linguistic / typological** method grounds the theory; (d) **non-reductionist** internal structure — only the part–whole relation between a construction and its elements, no constituency/dependency primitives. Upgrades the "Croft 2001; not in-repo" flag in [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md) to a sourced provenance, and is a **second `constructional`↔`distributional` hinge** (alongside Goldberg 2006's usage-based turn): in RCG *what a category is* is a distributional fact about constructions. **2001 book body UNREACHABLE as open access** (OUP catalogue metadata-only; Google-Books preview JS-walled, blurb only; archive.org has no scan at all) — **but quotes carried via Croft's own self-archived "Radical Construction Grammar" author manuscript** (UNM faculty page, `Elsevier-RadicalCxG.pdf`; fetched + text-extracted), **author-primary** text restating the book, with Croft's own book-page locators (unverified against the book; manuscript venue unconfirmed on its face). **Theory source, not a human anchor.** **status: secondary-only** (book body unread; logged 2026-06-25, session 109). `refines` [`concept/constructional-meaning`](base/concepts/constructional-meaning.md); `depends-on` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md). (**philosophical track / constructional line**)
- [`base/sources/evans-1973-causal-theory-of-names.md`](base/sources/evans-1973-causal-theory-of-names.md) — Evans 1973, "The Causal Theory of Names" (Part I of a 1973 Aristotelian Society symposium with Altham), *Proceedings of the Aristotelian Society* Suppl. Vol. 47:187-208 (self-archived JSTOR scan of the original; official OUP/JSTOR paywalled). The classic **critique-from-within** of the causal theory of reference and the second externalist primary the `referential.externalist` sub-tag rested on. Evans grants a causal element in name-reference but rejects the pure Kripkean **chain-back-to-baptism** picture: the **Madagascar** case shows reference can *shift* through the chain, so denotation tracks the **dominant causal source of the body of information** a community associates with the name (pp. 198-199, 202), under a **common-knowledge-in-a-community** name-hood condition (p. 202, "more stringent than Kripke's") plus a **deference** clause (p. 205). **Corrects the concept page's prior characterization** ("refers via a causal chain back to a baptismal event" — that is the view Evans *rejects*). `refines` [`source/putnam-1975-meaning-of-meaning`](base/sources/putnam-1975-meaning-of-meaning.md): Evans's *information-source* reference-fixer is a **different** externalist mechanism from Putnam's environment+expert+indexical triad — and (the reason the essays' trigger (c) was armed for Evans) his "source" relation is satisfied by *reading a person's works* (p. 199), a **textual** transmission hook absent from Putnam, though paired with knowledge-aptness (p. 200) and intentions/common-knowledge (p. 202) conditions a deflationist would deny a text model. **Theory source, not a human anchor** (a 1973 philosophy essay; silent on machines; licenses no human-comparison claim). **status: received** (Evans's Part I read in full; page-level quotes verified character-for-character against the OCR-extracted scan, OCR artifacts flagged inline, 2026-06-25, session 111). `supports` [`concept/referential-meaning`](base/concepts/referential-meaning.md). (**referential / philosophical track**)
- [`base/sources/burge-1979-individualism-and-the-mental.md`](base/sources/burge-1979-individualism-and-the-mental.md) — Burge 1979, "Individualism and the Mental," *Midwest Studies in Philosophy* vol. 4:73-121 (open-access UCLA Philosophy PDF of the original typesetting, real digital text layer). The canonical statement of **social externalism / anti-individualism about mental content** — the social-externalist companion the concept page listed as "(not in-repo; characterization)." Where Putnam externalizes *natural-kind reference* via the environment, Burge externalizes the **contents of propositional attitudes themselves**, via the **arthritis** three-step thought experiment (pp. 77-79): two physically/phenomenally identical individuals have **different-content thoughts** solely because their **linguistic communities** use "arthritis" differently. Runs on *ordinary* words (artifact terms, color adjectives, abstract nouns, action verbs — p. 79), not only natural kinds. The load-bearing premise is **incomplete understanding** (a subject thinks *with* a notion he only partly grasps — p. 79) anchored by **deference** to specialists who "understand our terms better than we do" (p. 80); communal practice fixes content "even in cases where I fully understand" (p. 85). Makes the community-and-deference dependency the in-repo reference essays turn on **even more load-bearing** than Putnam (content, not just reference). Bears both ways on the corpus-membership antecedent (low individual-side bar pushes toward "could count"; the requirement of *attitudes* + corrigible *deference* pushes toward "could not") — **laid out, not decided**, on the page. **Theory source, not a human anchor** (a 1979 philosophy essay; predates LLMs; licenses no human-comparison claim). **status: received** (primary read in full; page-level quotes verified character-for-character against the digital text layer via PyMuPDF, one bracketed restoration flagged, 2026-06-25, session 111). `supports` [`concept/referential-meaning`](base/concepts/referential-meaning.md). (**referential / philosophical track**)
- [`base/sources/wittgenstein-1953-philosophical-investigations.md`](base/sources/wittgenstein-1953-philosophical-investigations.md) — Wittgenstein 1953, *Philosophische Untersuchungen* (*Philosophical Investigations*, posthumous; Blackwell); the **founding primary of the meaning-as-use pole** ([`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) pole b), closing that page's "not in-repo; characterization" Wittgenstein gap. Supplies verbatim locators for the three load-bearing ideas: **meaning-as-use** (§43, *with* its qualifying "large class of cases" clause that the memorized slogan drops), **language-games** in "an activity, or … a form of life" (§§7, 23), and **family resemblance** (§§66–67, the *game* example — the ancestor of prototype/graded-category structure the project's lexical-gradience finding maps onto). **Two-route open-access provenance, mixed strength:** §§43/7/66/67 **primary-direct** from the public-domain German (wittgensteinproject.org, PD notice on page); English §§43/23/66/201/243 **carried-via-secondary** through the OA Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy entry (the Anscombe English translation is in copyright and was **not** sourced; English glosses of the German are the project's own, marked); rule-following/private-language (§§201/243) at **lower strength** (secondary-only, no primary German fetched). **Theory primary, NOT a human anchor** (grounds the use-theory a model may instantiate, never a model result). **status: received** (all 12 quotes independently re-verified against the cited sources by the session's coherence pass, 2026-06-26, session 115). `supports` [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md); `depends-on` [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md) + [`concept/inferential-meaning`](base/concepts/inferential-meaning.md). (**philosophical track / use-meaning pole**)
- [`base/sources/tarski-1944-semantic-conception-of-truth.md`](base/sources/tarski-1944-semantic-conception-of-truth.md) — Tarski 1944, "The Semantic Conception of Truth and the Foundations of Semantics," *Philosophy and Phenomenological Research* 4(3):341-376 (Andrew Chrucky OA hypertext transcription; Part I, §§1-13). The **truth-conditional pole's machinery primary** — the apparatus [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) had cited only as "Tarski's recursive definition of truth via satisfaction (not in-repo)." Verbatim, section-located: the **material-adequacy condition / Convention T** and its schema **"(T) X is true if, and only if, p"** with the **"snow is white"** instance (§4); truth defined via **satisfaction** ("a sentence is true if it is satisfied by all objects," §11); the **object-language / meta-language** distinction and the **semantically-closed**-language diagnosis of the **Liar** antinomy (§§7-9); the Aristotelian gloss (§3). Caveat: the 1944 article *outlines* the satisfaction recursion the 1933 monograph gives in full (not read); locators are section-level (no PPR pagination on the host); one mirror typo quarantined. **Theory source, not a human anchor.** **status: received** (quotes grep-verified against the raw transcription, 2026-06-26, session 116). `supports` [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) + [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md). (**referential / philosophical track**)
- [`base/sources/davidson-1967-truth-and-meaning.md`](base/sources/davidson-1967-truth-and-meaning.md) — Davidson 1967, "Truth and Meaning," *Synthese* 17(3):304-323 (UH open-access mirror of the JSTOR journal scan; `pypdf` extraction, OCR cleanup flagged). The **founding statement of a truth-conditional *theory of meaning* for natural language** — the lineage member [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) had cited only as "(not in-repo; characterization)." Verbatim, page-located: **"to give truth conditions is a way of giving the meaning of a sentence"** (p. 310); the schema **"(T) s is T if and only if p"** (Davidson keeps the uninterpreted `is T`, the point of his borrow-then-identify move, p. 309); the **learnability/finitude** motivation (a finite theory for "a potential infinitude of sentences," p. 304); the **rejection of meanings-as-entities** ("they have no demonstrated use," p. 307); the **holism** line ("only in the context of the language does a sentence (and therefore a word) have meaning," p. 308); and the **Convention-T dependence** (pp. 309-310). Caveat: the *reversal* of Tarski's order of explanation (truth taken as primitive to illuminate meaning) is flagged as standard-reading interpretation, not a Davidson quote. **Theory source, not a human anchor.** **status: received** (quotes verified against the extraction, page locators off the scan footers, 2026-06-26, session 116). `supports` [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) + [`concept/semantic-holism`](base/concepts/semantic-holism.md) + [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md). (**referential / philosophical track**)
- [`base/sources/quine-1951-two-dogmas.md`](base/sources/quine-1951-two-dogmas.md) — Quine 1951, "Two Dogmas of Empiricism," *The Philosophical Review* 60(1):20-43 (ditext/Chrucky OA transcription, a 1951/1961 composite — flagged). The **headwater primary of confirmation holism** — the source [`concept/semantic-holism`](base/concepts/semantic-holism.md) called "the headwater" but had cited only as "(not in-repo; characterization)." Verbatim, section-located: the **two dogmas** (the analytic/synthetic cleavage + **reductionism**, §1); the **analyticity/synonymy circle** ("'synonymy' which is no less in need of clarification than analyticity itself," §§1/4); **confirmation holism** ("our statements about the external world face the tribunal of sense experience not individually but only as a corporate body"; "The unit of empirical significance is the whole of science," §§5-6); the **field-of-force** metaphor (§6) and "no statement is immune to revision" (§6). Caveat: Quine 1951 does **not** itself argue the holism→compositionality threat (that is Fodor & Lepore, not-in-repo); locators are section-level (no PR pagination on the host); composite-edition + stray-space artifacts flagged. **Theory source, not a human anchor.** **status: received** (quotes grep-verified against the transcription, 2026-06-26, session 116). `supports` [`concept/semantic-holism`](base/concepts/semantic-holism.md) + [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md). (**philosophical track / holism pole**)
- [`base/sources/dummett-1975-what-is-a-theory-of-meaning.md`](base/sources/dummett-1975-what-is-a-theory-of-meaning.md) — Dummett 1975/76, "What is a Theory of Meaning?" (I in Guttenplan ed., *Mind and Language*; II in Evans & McDowell eds., *Truth and Meaning*; read from the 1993 *Seas of Language* reprint chs. 1–2 via a `free.fr` full-text mirror, pdfminer extraction). The **founding statement of semantic molecularism** — the middle position [`concept/semantic-holism`](base/concepts/semantic-holism.md) had cited only as "(not in-repo; characterization)." Verbatim, page-located to the reprint's own `end p.N` markers (mixed strength, all flagged per-quote): **primary-strength** — the molecularist conclusion ("must accord with an atomistic, or at least a molecular, conception of language, not a holistic one," essay I p. 21), the **piecemeal-learning argument** against holism ("can make no sense of the idea of knowing part of a language," essay I p. 32), the **atomistic/molecular definition** (per-word axiom vs. whole-sentence theorem, essay II p. 37), and the **manifestation requirement** (essay II p. 41); **secondary-strength** (via SEP "Meaning Holism" §2.2) — the **Fodor & Lepore "unstable resting point" objection** and the **analytic/synthetic connection** re-invoking Quine. Caveats: pagination is the 1993 reprint's, **not** the original 1975/76 venues; mirror legality not vouched for (short fair-use quotes only); the "fully manifest in use" sharpening flagged as Dummett's *later* (1993+) formulation. **Theory source, NOT a human anchor** (grounds the molecularist *theory* a model may instantiate, never a model result; the manifestation→LLM connection is the project's interpretive bridge, marked as such). **status: received** (Q1–Q4 verified char-for-char against the extracted text, 2026-06-26, session 119). `refines` [`concept/semantic-holism`](base/concepts/semantic-holism.md); `depends-on` [`source/quine-1951-two-dogmas`](base/sources/quine-1951-two-dogmas.md). (**philosophical track / molecularism — middle of the holism axis**)
- [`base/sources/rosch-mervis-1975-family-resemblances.md`](base/sources/rosch-mervis-1975-family-resemblances.md) — Rosch & Mervis 1975, "Family resemblances: Studies in the internal structure of categories," *Cognitive Psychology* 7(4):573-605 (University-of-Colorado course-page scan of the original; `pdftotext`, OCR artifacts "criterial"→"criteria1" and "p < .001"→"p < .OOl" flagged). The **prototype / graded-category primary** that turned Wittgenstein's family-resemblance idea into a quantitative result — discharges (at **full primary strength**) one of the two prototype legs [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md) had carried as "(not in-repo; characterization)." Verbatim, page-located: the criterial-features target it overturns (pp. 573-574); the **family-resemblance set-theoretic definition** taken explicitly "from Wittgenstein (1953)" (pp. 574-575); the **attribute-overlap scoring method** (pp. 581-582); the load-bearing result — six per-category Spearman correlations between family-resemblance score and rated typicality, **0.84-0.94, all p < .001** (Table 2, p. 582); and the closing verdict that the study is "an empirical confirmation of Wittgenstein's (1953) argument that formal criteria are neither a logical nor psychological necessity" (p. 605). In-copyright (© 1975 Academic Press); short fair-use quotes only. **Theory / empirical-psychology primary, NOT a human anchor** (it predates LLMs and grounds the prototype *theory*, never a model result; the project's graded human yardstick stays the DURel/Usim resource). **status: received** (all quotes character-verified against the scan, journal pagination, 2026-06-26, session 117). `refines` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md) + [`source/wittgenstein-1953-philosophical-investigations`](base/sources/wittgenstein-1953-philosophical-investigations.md) (the experiment operationalizes §§66-67). (**philosophical track / prototype line**)
- [`base/sources/rosch-1975-cognitive-representations.md`](base/sources/rosch-1975-cognitive-representations.md) — Rosch 1975, "Cognitive Representations of Semantic Categories," *Journal of Experimental Psychology: General* 104(3):192-233 (DOI 10.1037/0096-3445.104.3.192). The **other half of the prototype backbone** (priming/verification experiments: reliable graded typicality ratings; advance category-name primes facilitate matching for typical members and inhibit it for atypical ones; fuzzy boundaries) — narrows the second prototype leg of [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md)'s "(not in-repo)" flag to **secondary strength**. The **OA primary is authoritatively unreachable** (Unpaywall `oa_status: closed`, `oa_locations: []`; Semantic Scholar `CLOSED`; academia.edu/CORE/scispace 403 or Cloudflare-walled), so the findings are **carried-via-secondary** through Rosch's own 1978 "Principles of Categorization" retrospective (OA cs.rice.edu scan), with every finding pinned to the **1975b** citation key resolved from that chapter's reference list — **no page within 192-233 asserted as read.** **Theory / empirical-psychology primary, NOT a human anchor.** The `supports` link to [`result/lexical-sense-gradience-v1`](findings/results/lexical-sense-gradience-v1.md) is **theory-grounding only** — that result's human anchor remains its DURel/Usim resource, not this source. **status: secondary-only** (deliberate non-standard status string — OA primary unreachable; the Rosch 1975 *primary* stays wanted; logged 2026-06-26, session 117). `refines` [`concept/frame-and-prototype-semantics`](base/concepts/frame-and-prototype-semantics.md); `supports` [`result/lexical-sense-gradience-v1`](findings/results/lexical-sense-gradience-v1.md). (**philosophical track / prototype line**)
- [`base/sources/lewis-1970-general-semantics.md`](base/sources/lewis-1970-general-semantics.md) — Lewis 1970, "General Semantics," *Synthese* 22(1-2):18-67 (David K. Lewis papers author-estate self-archive, andrewmbailey.com; scan of the *Synthese* original; `pdftotext`, OCR corrections flagged). The **Markerese argument** primary: translating English into a formal markup ("Semantic Markerese") is **not yet a semantics**, because one can know the Markerese translation "without knowing the first thing about the meaning … namely, the conditions under which it would be true" (pp. 18-19) — a form-vs-meaning point the project reads against the question of whether a symbol-manipulating LLM thereby has meaning (flagged in-page as the project's interpretive application, **not** a Lewis claim). Also captures meaning-determines-truth-conditions (pp. 22-23), intension-as-function (pp. 23-25), and the **compositional** interpreted-phrase-marker tree (pp. 31-33). In-copyright (© 1970 D. Reidel); short fair-use quotes only. **Theory primary, NOT a human anchor.** **status: received** (Markerese passage + others character-verified against the scan, *Synthese* pagination, 2026-06-26, session 117). `refines` [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md); `supports` [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md). (**philosophical track / truth-conditional pole**)
- [`base/sources/janssen-zimmermann-montague-semantics-sep.md`](base/sources/janssen-zimmermann-montague-semantics-sep.md) — Janssen & Zimmermann 2025, *Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy* (Spring 2025 archived edition; first pub. Nov 7 2011, subst. rev. Feb 5 2025), "Montague Semantics"; the **open-access reference survey** that discharges the last not-in-repo leg of the truth-conditional lineage — the **Montague** characterization both [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md) (§1, the homomorphism-from-a-syntactic-algebra-to-a-semantic-algebra picture) and [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md) (Honest gaps: "only **Montague (PTQ 1973)** remains not in-repo") had carried only as "characterization." Ten verbatim §-located quotes (double-fetch-confirmed across the live + Spring-2025-archived URLs): compositionality plain (§1.2) and in its algebraic form ("Syntax is an algebra, semantics is an algebra, and meaning is a homomorphism between them," §3.2); the model-theoretic/denotational core (truth-in-a-model + entailment-over-all-models, §§1.1/1.2); natural-language-as-formal-language ("no important theoretical difference … the study of natural language belonged to mathematics, and not to psychology," §1.1); the **rule-to-rule hypothesis** (§§1.2/2.3); context-dependence pushed to pragmatics (§3.4). **Secondary-only**: every quote is the SEP survey reporting/selecting Montague (one — the §1.1 "in my opinion" sentence — is Montague's own words quoted *by* the survey), **not** a primary ingestion; **PTQ 1973** and the 1970 companion papers ("Universal Grammar"/"English as a Formal Language") stay **not in-repo / wanted**. **Framing source, NOT a human anchor** (formal-semantics survey of human language; no labeled resource; makes no `anchors:` claim). **status: received** (ten quotes double-fetch-verified, authors + dates read off the entry, 2026-06-27, session 124). `depends-on` [`concept/compositionality`](base/concepts/compositionality.md) + [`concept/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning`](base/concepts/truth-conditional-and-use-meaning.md). (**philosophical track / truth-conditional pole**)
- [`base/sources/strasser-antonelli-nonmonotonic-logic-sep.md`](base/sources/strasser-antonelli-nonmonotonic-logic-sep.md) — Strasser & Antonelli 2024, *Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy* (Winter 2024 archived edition; first pub. Dec 11 2001, subst. rev. Nov 23 2024), "Non-monotonic Logic"; the **open-access reference survey** that fills the queued [P3] want flagged by [`conjecture/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md) — which had cast the add-vs-cancel pattern as monotone-accumulation-vs-defeasance **"by analogy only"** because no in-repo source treated non-monotonic/defeasible reasoning. Four verbatim §-located quotes (double-fetch-confirmed against the Winter-2024 archived URL): defeasible reasoning as retract-on-new-information (Introduction); the **monotony** property stated formally ("If Σ ⊨ φ then also Σ ∪ Σ′ ⊨ φ … consequence sets are robust under the addition of information," §1); non-monotonicity as consequences that "may not persist when new information is obtained" + the "most/typical/etc." defeasible support (§1); and **specificity-override of a default** ("More specific information overrides more generic information," §3.2 inheritance networks). **Encyclopedia-survey strength** (honestly tertiary): grounds the **formal vocabulary** the conjecture/essay use — upgrading the mapping from "analogy only" to "grounded in a survey source" — but the **primary literature** (Reiter 1980 Default Logic, McCarthy circumscription 1980/1986, McDermott & Doyle 1980, KLM 1990) is summarized, **not in-repo**, and stays wanted. **Framing source, NOT a human anchor** (formal-logic survey, no labeled resource; never discharges a result's human-anchor obligation; does NOT identify LLM cancellation *as* technical non-monotonic inference — that stays the conjecture's open question). **status: received** (four quotes verbatim-verified, authors + dates read off the entry, 2026-06-28, session 131). `depends-on` [`concept/inferential-meaning`](base/concepts/inferential-meaning.md). (**philosophical track / inferential pole**)
- [`base/sources/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge.md`](base/sources/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge.md) — Cao, Yamada, Teufel & Tokunaga 2025, *Language Resources & Evaluation* (arXiv 2412.01131; **v5, the peer-reviewed published version**); "A Comprehensive Evaluation of Semantic Relation Knowledge of Pretrained Language Models and Humans". The **first in-repo empirical, human-compared, multi-relation** treatment of the lexical sense-relation vocabulary (hypernymy/hyponymy/holonymy/meronymy/antonymy/synonymy) — partially filling the gap [`concept/polysemy`](base/concepts/polysemy.md) "Honest gaps" flags (carried so far only via [`source/cruse-1986-lexical-semantics`](base/sources/cruse-1986-lexical-semantics.md) at secondary strength). A same-task prompt-based probe answered by **both six PLMs (four masked: BERT/RoBERTa base+large; two causal: Llama-3 8B/70B) and 48 MTurk annotators**; headline a "significant knowledge gap between humans and models for all semantic relations," **antonymy the lone outlier** where models do well, and **causal LMs not reliably beating masked LMs**. **Prior-art + methodology + candidate human-comparison resource — NOT a direct comparison to the project's frontier panel** (older/smaller models) and **NOT an adopted anchor**: the released `hancules/ProbeResponses` human data (open-ended noun-relata production, categorical not graded) has resource *potential* but carries two pre-adoption blockers — **no LICENSE file** and a **10,507-vs-10,546 probe-count discrepancy** — so cataloguing it as a `resource`/anchor is a separate cross-session step. **Version caveat:** cite v5 only (v1's "16 PLMs / asymmetry metric / MLMs-win" figures are superseded). **status: received** (abstract + body quotes verified character-for-character against the v5 HTML; section locators, no journal page numbers; coherence-pass re-verified, 2026-06-29, session 145). `supports` [`concept/polysemy`](base/concepts/polysemy.md); `depends-on` [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md); `refines` [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md). (**lexical line / human-comparison**)
- [`base/sources/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations.md`](base/sources/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations.md) — Diera & Scherp 2026, **LREC 2026** (arXiv 2603.17624, accepted); "Do Language Models Encode Semantic Relations? Probing and Sparse Feature Analysis". A **representational / mechanistic-interpretability** probe of four WordNet lexical relations (synonymy, antonymy, hypernymy, hyponymy) in three decoder-only models (Pythia-70M, GPT-2, Llama 3.1 8B), via linear probing + sparse autoencoders + activation patching. Headline a **directional asymmetry**: hypernymy encoded redundantly / suppression-resistant, hyponymy carried by compact features more disrupted by ablation; relation signal peaks mid-layer in post-residual/MLP pathways; causal patching robust only at Llama-8B scale; difficulty ordering antonymy-easiest → synonymy-hardest. The **inside-the-model companion** to the project's behavioral lexical wedge — catalogued as a **map and interpretability-side counterpoint** (alongside [`source/beckmann-queloz-2025-mechanistic-indicators`](base/sources/beckmann-queloz-2025-mechanistic-indicators.md) and [`source/milliere-buckner-2024-philosophical-intro-ii`](base/sources/milliere-buckner-2024-philosophical-intro-ii.md)), **not** a method the project uses, **not** evidence about its behavioral findings, **not a human anchor** (WordNet schema, no human-judgment instrument), and with **no transfer** to the frontier panel. **Do not conflate** its representational hypernymy/hyponymy asymmetry with the project's behavioral **add-vs-cancel monotonicity** asymmetry (different phenomena, different levels — at most a flagged surface resonance). **status: received** (abstract + 9 load-bearing quotes verified character-for-character against the arXiv HTML; section locators; coherence-pass re-verified, 2026-06-29, session 145). `refines` [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md); `supports` [`concept/polysemy`](base/concepts/polysemy.md). (**lexical line / representational counterpoint**)
- [`base/sources/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence.md`](base/sources/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence.md) — Justeson & Katz 1991, *Computational Linguistics* 17(1):1-20 (ACL Anthology open-access scan J91-1001; embedded OCR layer extracted with PyMuPDF, hyphenation/page-boundaries flagged). The **primary corpus-linguistic study** of *where* antonyms occur relative to each other (extending Charles & Miller 1989; J&K's own first contribution is the syntactic-frame analysis): on the 1M-word Brown Corpus, **antonymous (predicative) adjectives co-occur in the same sentence far above chance** (p. 3) and overwhelmingly in **syntactically parallel, lexically near-identical contrastive frames** — conjoined "X and Y" and repeated phrases with one antonym substituted for the other ("63% (139/219) … in lexically identical structures", "Fully 164 (75%) … in conjoined syntactic structures", §3, pp. 11-12). The **primary anchor** for the contrastive-frame premise the antonymy-as-shadow line had carried only via Harris; **confirms** (does not complicate) it. **Scope/limits: predicative adjectives, one ~1961 corpus, a psycholinguistic *acquisition* theory, pre-LLM — a fact about the *training distribution*, NOT an LLM/panel result and NOT a human anchor**; with Charles & Miller it *denies* free global substitutability (substitution is within co-occurrence sentences); adjectival→nominal extension is extrapolation. **status: received** (all quotes verified verbatim against the OCR layer; *CL* 17(1) page locators from scan footers, 2026-06-29, session 148). `supports` [`essay/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md); `refines` [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md); `depends-on` [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md). (**lexical line / distributional primary**)
- [`base/sources/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy.md`](base/sources/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy.md) — Cao, Yamada & Tokunaga 2025, **\*SEM 2025** (arXiv 2509.11534, cs.CL, accepted); "On the Distinctive Co-occurrence Characteristics of Antonymy". The **cross-PoS / cross-relation companion** to the adjective-only J&K primary, by the **same group** as [`source/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge`](base/sources/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge.md) (the model-side antonymy-outlier paper). A **corpus-only** study on **COCA** (17.7M sentences) measuring antonym co-occurrence **strength (G²), order, and distance** against three other relations (synonymy / hyper-hyponymy / holo-meronymy) + an unrelated control, across **nouns/verbs/adjectives/adverbs**. Headline: antonymy is "**distinctive in three respects: … high strength, … a preferred linear order, and … short spans**" (Abstract) and "**consistently distinctive from all other relations across all metrics**" (§6) — **highest G² across all PoS** (§4), the **only consistent order preference**, the **shortest span**; nominal antonymy the strongest (G²=11,144, with disclosed ('child','parent')/('man','woman') >100k outliers, §4). Supplies the **cross-relation cue-strength measurement J&K lacked** and **extends antonym co-occurrence beyond adjectives** (fires [`essay/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md)'s trigger (d) a *second* time, confirming the nominal extrapolation's *strength* leg). Authors themselves connect it to the PLM "**antonymy bias**" as a possible pretraining "**shortcut**" needing disentangling (§1, §5) — convergent with the project's shadow reading. **Scope/limits: a corpus statistic, NOT a model/panel result and NOT a human anchor; lemma+PoS level, no WSD; explicitly "can not answer in which lexical and dependency constructions two words … occur" (Limitations) — so the parallel-contrastive-frame mechanism for nouns stays inferential (authors only *speculate* it); the "antonymy bias" it cites is non-frontier PLMs (BERT/RoBERTa/Llama-3), no transfer to the panel.** **status: received** (all quotes verified character-for-character against the v1 HTML; section locators, no page numbers; arXiv non-exclusive license, 2026-06-30, session 149). `supports` [`essay/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md) + [`conjecture/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation`](findings/conjectures/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation.md); `refines` [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md); `depends-on` [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md). (**lexical line / distributional primary, cross-relation**)

### Base — resources

- [`base/resources/index.md`](base/resources/index.md) — catalog of human-anchored empirical resources.
- [`base/resources/clark-wilkes-gibbs-1986-referring.md`](base/resources/clark-wilkes-gibbs-1986-referring.md) — **Clark & Wilkes-Gibbs 1986**, *Cognition* 22(1):1–39, "Referring as a collaborative process"; the **ratified empirical anchor** for the relational axis (decision [`decisions/resolved/relational-anchor-shortlist`](decisions/resolved/relational-anchor-shortlist.md), Option A) — the canonical **tangram-naming convergence** paradigm: dyads collaboratively coin and **compress** shared labels over rounds (41→8 words/figure, F(1,35)=44.31, p<.001; 3.7→~1 turns/figure), via an acceptance cycle governed by a **Principle of Mutual Responsibility**. A **candidate human anchor** (`anchor: candidate`), NOT yet ratified-as-anchor for any specific result. Honest limit recorded in-page: it grounds human collaborative referential **convergence/entrainment** and its interactive source, **NOT** order-sensitivity/commutativity of conventions (it varies repetition and re-randomizes positions but never scrambles a fixed interaction history) — that discriminator stays the project's own humanly-unanchored wedge; partner-specificity is [`source/brennan-clark-1996-conceptual-pacts`](base/sources/brennan-clark-1996-conceptual-pacts.md), not this. **status: received** (2026-06-28, session 134; primary-direct full text from Clark's Stanford self-archive; 8 quotes verified char-for-char with journal pagination; OCR artifacts flagged). (**relational axis**)
- [`base/resources/subtlex-us-frequency.md`](base/resources/subtlex-us-frequency.md) — **SUBTLEX-US word-frequency norm** (Brysbaert & New 2009; 74,286 word forms from a 51M-word subtitle corpus; `Lg10WF` = log10 word-form frequency). Status: **catalogued** (plain-text list fetched + sha256-pinned this session; no formal license string — recipe-not-corpus: full list gitignored, `prep.py` + a derived seed table committed). The **Q1 frequency-matching floor** for [`conjecture/function-word-substitutability`](findings/conjectures/function-word-substitutability.md), governed by [`decisions/resolved/function-word-anchor-design`](decisions/resolved/function-word-anchor-design.md) (**ratified 2026-06-21**). Grounds the matching *control*, not the indicator (no PoS/acceptability/entailment). (created 2026-06-21)
- [`base/resources/languageR-dative-corpus.md`](base/resources/languageR-dative-corpus.md) — **Bresnan et al. (2007) dative-alternation corpus** (`languageR::dative`; GPL; 3263 attested ditransitive clauses coded for the information-structure factors — given/accessible/new, pronominality, definiteness, animacy, length — plus the NP/PP outcome). Documentation + license verified verbatim from CRAN; **mirrored + inspected firsthand 2026-06-20 (status catalogued)** — 3263×15 confirmed, NP(DOC)=2414/PP(PD)=849, factor levels confirmed, logistic fit reproduces the canonical human directions (acc 0.887). Anchors [`conjecture/dative-alternation-information-structure`](findings/conjectures/dative-alternation-information-structure.md); the build is governed by [`decisions/resolved/dative-anchor-and-indicator`](decisions/resolved/dative-anchor-and-indicator.md) (**ratified 2026-06-20, ADOPT MODIFIED** — corpus production surface adopted as primary anchor). (created 2026-06-20)
- [`base/resources/mahowald-2023-aann-stimuli.md`](base/resources/mahowald-2023-aann-stimuli.md) — Mahowald 2023 EACL AANN stimulus suite + MTurk acceptability ratings (status: **catalogued** 2026-06-12 — repo mirrored, MIT license verified, Exp-2 item-level ratings confirmed usable); anchor for [`conjecture/aann-construction`](findings/conjectures/aann-construction.md).
- [`base/resources/wic-graded-usage-similarity.md`](base/resources/wic-graded-usage-similarity.md) — Usim graded usage-similarity ratings (Erk, McCarthy & Gaylord 2009/2013) — graded 5-point human usage-similarity judgments; the candidate gradience anchor for [`conjecture/lexical-sense-gradience`](findings/conjectures/lexical-sense-gradience.md), with WiC (Pilehvar & Camacho-Collados 2019, binary, CC BY-NC 4.0) as the binary cross-check. Status: external-only (license/counts unverified this run — see page). (created 2026-05-29)
- [`base/resources/wic-word-in-context.md`](base/resources/wic-word-in-context.md) — **WiC (Word-in-Context, Pilehvar & Camacho-Collados 2019, NAACL; CC BY-NC 4.0).** **Verified live 2026-05-31** (package fetched + inspected; sha256 pinned): **binary** lexicographer same/different-sense labels over two contexts of a target word, 7,466 items (50/50, N+V, 2,345 targets; the pilehvar package **ships test gold labels**). Negatives are **homonymy-enriched** (closest-polyseme pairs pruned) — the discreteness contrast DWUG EN lacked. Scope limit: **binary, not graded** (no DURel-median correlation). Anchors the clause-(b) lexical-v3 ([`design/lexical-polysemy-homonymy-v3`](../experiments/designs/lexical-polysemy-homonymy-v3.md)) **and** the image probe ([`design/multimodal-grounding-image-v1`](../experiments/designs/multimodal-grounding-image-v1.md)). (created 2026-05-31)
- [`base/resources/semeval2017-pun-corpus.md`](base/resources/semeval2017-pun-corpus.md) — **SemEval-2017 Task 7 pun corpus** (Miller, Hempelmann & Gurevych 2017; mixed CC BY 4.0 / CC BY-NC 4.0; fetched + sha256-hashed + inspected firsthand 2026-06-23). ~1298 homographic + ~1098 heterographic puns with **human per-item gold of the two WordNet 3.1 senses each pun evokes, on the actual sentence** — human sense **co-activation** labels for genuine forced-both items (the in-item evidence SemCor's general-usage proxy could not give). Anchor for the forced-both line (gate Q4) + the matched-ambiguity Option-A homonym sense-anchor; **anchor RATIFIED for Q4 co-activation only, session 93** ([`decisions/resolved/sense-coactivation-anchor-semeval-puns`](decisions/resolved/sense-coactivation-anchor-semeval-puns.md); Q-A adopt / Q-B-1 separate dominance step owed / Q-C-1 puns as forced-both stimuli, homonym subset, frozen). Honest limit: certifies co-*presence*, not graded balance/dominance. (catalogued 2026-06-23, session 92)
- [`base/resources/homonym-meaning-dominance-norms.md`](base/resources/homonym-meaning-dominance-norms.md) — **Homonym meaning-dominance norms** (British eDom, Maciejewski & Klepousniotou 2016, 10.5334/jopd.28; + spoken-ambiguity norms, J. Cognition 10.5334/joc.194; both **CC BY 4.0**, licenses + OSF reachability + schema verified by direct fetch 2026-06-23). Per-**word** human sense-balance/dominance (D≈0 = balanced) for *selecting* balanced homonyms — the human-anchored balance/dominance step the [`decisions/resolved/sense-coactivation-anchor-semeval-puns`](decisions/resolved/sense-coactivation-anchor-semeval-puns.md) Q-B-1 calls for (ratified session 93 — a separate dominance step is owed since co-activation ≠ no-dominance); a CC-BY upgrade over the SemCor general-balance proxy. **General-usage, not the specific sentence's** balance → softens-not-eliminates the forced-both Q1-ii in-item gap; data not yet fetched. (catalogued 2026-06-23, session 92)
- [`base/resources/wordnet-sense-inventory.md`](base/resources/wordnet-sense-inventory.md) — **Princeton WordNet** (Miller 1995 / Fellbaum 1998; permissive WordNet 3.0 License, verified verbatim from the NLTK-shipped LICENSE). The expert-lexicographer **synset** sense inventory (117,659 synsets / 82,115 noun; verified via NLTK). The categorical same/different-sense backbone the op-gate Q2 + v2/v3 stratification assume; anchors the image probe's constructed pairs (gold = same vs different synset). Honest grain: categorical lexicographic partition, **not** graded (DWUG) nor per-item human labels (WiC). (created 2026-05-31)
- [`base/resources/dwug-usage-graphs.md`](base/resources/dwug-usage-graphs.md) — DWUG (Diachronic Word Usage Graphs, Schlechtweg et al.): graded human usage-similarity judgments in the DURel/Usim tradition; evaluated this session as the ratified **Option-B** graded-anchor candidate for [`conjecture/lexical-sense-gradience`](findings/conjectures/lexical-sense-gradience.md) — see the page for the license / scale / counts / fetchability / fit verification breakdown. (created 2026-05-30)
- [`base/resources/lancaster-sensorimotor-norms.md`](base/resources/lancaster-sensorimotor-norms.md) — Lancaster Sensorimotor Norms (Lynott et al. 2020, **CC BY 4.0**): human perceptual/action strength ratings (0–5) on 11 sensorimotor dimensions for 39,707 English words; **fetched + checksummed this session** (sha256 pinned; full CSV gitignored, derived 42-lemma join table committed). The text-side perceptual-grounding **moderator** for prediction 1 of [`conjecture/multimodal-lexical-grounding-divergence`](findings/conjectures/multimodal-lexical-grounding-divergence.md) — a $0 join to the existing DWUG lexical result. Word-level (not sense-level); bears on prediction 1 only, not the image predictions. (created 2026-05-30; **multimodal axis**)
- [`base/resources/multimodal-anchor-scouting.md`](base/resources/multimodal-anchor-scouting.md) — **scouting note** (untyped, `wanted.md`-style; not yet a typed resource) on candidate human-anchored multimodal/grounded resources. Verified license/fetchability/meaning-bearing for 6 candidates; headline: **Lancaster Sensorimotor Norms** (CC BY 4.0) as a $0 text-side perceptual-grounding moderator on the existing DWUG lexical result, and **THINGS-data** (CC0) for an image-grounded probe; Winoground/SNLI-VE dropped (gated/auto-derived). (created 2026-05-30; **multimodal axis**)
- [`base/resources/vwsd-semeval-2023.md`](base/resources/vwsd-semeval-2023.md) — **VWSD (SemEval-2023 Task 1, Raganato et al. 2023)** — the **image-native** word-sense-disambiguation anchor [`conjecture/distributional-saturation-grounding-headroom`](findings/conjectures/distributional-saturation-grounding-headroom.md) named (but no session had scouted) for its text-under-determined stratum: pick 1 of 10 images for an ambiguous word given minimal context (EN/IT/FA). **Human gold = test (463 EN / 200 FA / 305 IT) + trial (16 EN)** (annotators authored the trigger words + curated the 9 distractors); **training (12,869 EN) is silver/automatic — not an anchor**. License **CC-BY-NC 4.0** (task-website only; scope unspecified; **image-redistribution UNCONFIRMED** — third-party image sources Wikidata/OmegaWiki/BabelPic). **Fetchable now** via Drive/OneDrive (572 MB resized test), no registration; **not fetched/checksummed this session**. Honest limit: gold is **binary correct-image selection, not a graded relatedness signal** — supplies selection-accuracy, *not* a drop-in for the conjecture's DURel-style graded DV. **The DV gate is now resolved** ([`decisions/resolved/vwsd-grounding-headroom-dv`](decisions/resolved/vwsd-grounding-headroom-dv.md), ratified s99 ADOPT MODIFIED: Option A, the selection-accuracy × text-separability *interaction* as test of record, tests the gating *shape* NOT prediction-1-as-written). **status: scouted + catalogued** (2026-06-24, session 97; **multimodal axis**)
- [`base/resources/things-data-triplets.md`](base/resources/things-data-triplets.md) — **THINGS-data behavioral triplet odd-one-out judgments (Hebart et al. 2023, eLife 12:e82580)** — scouted s99 as a candidate **graded** multimodal anchor (the "future graded-image resource" the VWSD DV ratification reserved for prediction-1-as-written). 4.70M human odd-one-out similarity judgments (4,699,160) over 1,854 object concepts / 26,107 images, N=12,340. **Fit verdict: DOES NOT CLEANLY FIT (partial/adjacent)** — it supplies graded human *whole-object similarity* (which of three objects is most dissimilar), a **different construct** from the conjecture's graded *within-word sense relatedness with disambiguating images*; no same-word/different-sense pairs, no polysemy structure → **not** a drop-in for [`resource/dwug-usage-graphs`](base/resources/dwug-usage-graphs.md)'s graded sense anchor. Right *shape* (graded + image + human + multi-rater), wrong *axis* (object similarity ≠ sense relatedness). Could legitimately anchor a distinct **representational-alignment** question or serve as PD/CC0 stimulus scaffolding (via THINGSplus). License honesty: behavioral data **reported CC0 but NOT primary-verified** (OSF node_license=null; Figshare+ 403'd); base THINGS **images are academic-use-only/restricted** (THINGSplus supplies PD/CC0 images) — do not conflate. Not fetched/checksummed. **status: scouted** (2026-06-24, session 99; **multimodal axis**)
- [`base/resources/scivetti-2025-cxnli-dataset.md`](base/resources/scivetti-2025-cxnli-dataset.md) — Scivetti et al. 2025 CxNLI / CxNLI-Distinction constructional NLI dataset (435 + 99 triples over 8 / 5 constructions; native-speaker baseline ≈0.90 / ≈0.83). Status: partial (de-anonymized repo inspected 2026-05-29: per-item construction labels + single gold answer per item). **Ratified anchor (2026-05-29)** for the caused-motion, conative, way, and comparative-correlative conjectures — answer-key + aggregate baseline. (created 2026-05-29)
- [`base/resources/hawkins-tangrams.md`](base/resources/hawkins-tangrams.md) — **Hawkins/Stanford tangrams repeated-reference corpus** (Hawkins, Frank & Goodman 2020, *Cognitive Science*; GitHub `license: null` + authors' "open corpus" statement). **Fetched + verified 2026-05-31** (sha256 `db8cee9d…`, 3.13 MB, 17,431 messages / 137 dyads / repetitions 1–6; raw gitignored, derived aggregate entrainment table committed under the **recipe-not-corpus** posture). Carries **ordered per-dyad referring-expression histories** with role/success/length — the human entrainment/compression curve (length 7.73→4.10 words, accuracy 0.78→0.94 over 6 reps) the relational pilot's convergence baseline needs. **Anchors the human convergence baseline only** — the pilot's novel live-vs-shuffled *trajectory-dependence* measure is **not** anchored by Hawkins. Catalogued per [`decisions/resolved/relational-fetchable-anchor`](decisions/resolved/relational-fetchable-anchor.md) (Option A). (created 2026-05-31)
- [`base/resources/blimp.md`](base/resources/blimp.md) — **BLiMP (Benchmark of Linguistic Minimal Pairs, Warstadt et al. 2020, TACL 8; CC-BY, README-prose only).** 67 paradigms × 1,000 = **67,000** template-generated English acceptability minimal pairs over 12 phenomena (incl. determiner-noun agreement, quantifiers, NPI licensing, subject-verb agreement); **96.4% aggregate human agreement** (distinct from the 89% baseline the Mahowald source quotes — kept separate). Status: **catalogued** (67 data files fetched + field schema inspected firsthand; a 10-line sample sha256-pinned, full set re-fetchable not committed). CAN supply a human-**acceptability** forced-choice backing — the optional **Posture-2 upgrade** named in [`decisions/resolved/function-word-anchor-design`](decisions/resolved/function-word-anchor-design.md) (overlaps the swap targets via determiner-noun agreement / quantifiers / NPI), and an adjacent baseline for the AANN line; **CANNOT** anchor entailment/implicature/sense-similarity (acceptability ≠ inference) and is template-generated (contamination caveat). (created 2026-06-21)
- [`base/resources/scalar-implicature-anchor-scouting.md`](base/resources/scalar-implicature-anchor-scouting.md) — **scouting page** (front-mattered) for a human-grounded **scalar-implicature / quantifier-interpretation** anchor for [`essay/function-words-not-one-category`](findings/essays/function-words-not-one-category.md) trigger (b) (the few→many "Many X → All X" split, [`result/function-word-few-many-split`](findings/results/function-word-few-many-split.md)). Scouted van Tiel et al. 2016 scalar-diversity (on-target quantifier `<some,all>` rate, but paywalled / OA PDF 403), Pankratz & van Tiel 2025 (CC BY but adjectival, off-target), VAQUUM quantifier appropriateness (close but appropriateness ≠ implicature-rate, rating license unverified), and the in-repo Scivetti CxNLI (single gold label, no quantifiers). **Honest null:** no clean openly-licensed quantifier-specific human implicature-rate set found → trigger (b)'s human-comparison upgrade stays blocked; `internal-contrast-only` remains the honest posture. (created 2026-06-21)

### Findings — conjectures

- [`findings/conjectures/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation.md`](findings/conjectures/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation.md) — status: **proposed** (2026-06-29, session 146); `anchor: pending`; **the testable bet the [`essay/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md) spawns.** On a same-task six-relation relatum probe over the **project's panel** (claude-sonnet-4.6 / gpt-5.4-mini / gemini-3.5-flash) against a **co-occurrence / contrastive-frame distributional control**, **antonymy is the relation whose competence is *least separable* from the control** (smallest over-and-above-the-shadow residual), while meronymy/hyponymy retain a larger residual; equivalently the raw-recovery ranking tracks distributional-cue strength. A lexical-pole instance of the continuum's "beat the distributional shadow" test, with the bet that one relation **most fails to**. Explicit confirm (smallest residual for antonymy and/or recovery-tracks-cue-strength, ≥2/3 models, direction-only) / falsify (antonymy keeps a large residual, or a weakly-cued relation like meronymy is recovered best) criteria, plus a named non-falsifying flat-residual null. **Recorded, not run** — three blockers: spend-bearing panel probe; **no adopted human anchor** (Cao's `ProbeResponses` is a *candidate* resource — no LICENSE file + a 10,507/10,546 count discrepancy — adoption is a separate cross-session `resource`-page step); and **no transfer** from the prior art (neither Cao nor Diera tested the panel). No `decisions/open/` entry opened. **s149: clause-2's distributional-cue-strength premise gained a direct cross-relation corpus measurement** ([`source/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy`](base/sources/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy.md): antonymy distinctively highest co-occurrence on COCA) — grounds the corpus-side premise, does **not** unblock (blockers stand). `depends-on` [`essay/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md) + [`source/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge`](base/sources/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge.md) + [`source/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy`](base/sources/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy.md) + [`source/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations`](base/sources/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations.md) + [`source/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence`](base/sources/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence.md) + [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md) + [`concept/inferential-meaning`](base/concepts/inferential-meaning.md); `refines` [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md); `contingent-on: []`. Directional claim: a VLM *given disambiguating images* produces graded sense-relatedness behavior **closer to the human DURel signal** than the same family's *text-only* behavior — concentrated where senses are **perceptually distinguishable** — beyond what the text distribution already supplies; the **text-only baseline is the null to beat**, with a *redundancy null* ("text already had it") and a *distraction null* both first-class. - [`findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md) — status: **tested** (proposed 2026-05-31; → tested 2026-06-28, session 137 — a **WEAK CONFIRM**); **the project's own ORIGINAL conjecture**, abstracting the recurring add/cancel pattern across the argument-structure results into a **monotonicity asymmetry**: current decoders readily *license* a construction-contributed (added) inference but resist *suppressing* a lexically-default one — better at monotone accumulation than at defeasance. De-confounded from ceiling by [`result/conative-cancel-direction-v2`](findings/results/conative-cancel-direction-v2.md) (about direction, not ceiling); both directions bounded ([`result/coercion-implicit-cue-v2b`](findings/results/coercion-implicit-cue-v2b.md)). Mechanism labeled speculation (distributional-prior-compatible). **Decisive matched-difficulty test RAN s137** ([`result/monotonicity-c2-battery-v1`](findings/results/monotonicity-c2-battery-v1.md)): after a C1 telic-completion B2 NO-GO, the C2 privative cancel arm (B2 GO) paired with the frozen resultative add arm → add licensing uniform-ceiling (1.00, 3/3), privative suppression partial (cancel_no_cue 0.75/0.625/0.875), asymmetry positive 3/3 and ≥20 pp in 2/3, cancel more instrument-fragile in 2/3 → **CONFIRMS by the frozen rule** (advances to `tested`, supported on this leg). **Weak/heavily caveated:** spans a deliberate verbal-add/nominal-cancel **domain mismatch** (M2), marginal in 2/3 models, leave-one-out-sensitive to two pre-flagged borderline privatives (toy violin, plastic apple). **CLEAN WITHIN-VERBAL CONFIRM — M2 DISCHARGED (s141):** the within-verbal battery ([`result/monotonicity-within-verbal-battery-v1`](findings/results/monotonicity-within-verbal-battery-v1.md)) paired the frozen resultative ADD arm with a **verbal** progressive CANCEL arm (causative-inchoative; B2 default s139, suppression s140) → B2 GO, asymmetry +0.50/+0.33/+0.67 ≥0.20 in **3/3**, fragility 3/3, cue robust, **leave-one-out robust at the verdict level** — so the generalization criterion is met by a NEW verbal cancel construction on a clean within-verbal contrast (suppression partial/verb-uneven: `shatter` resists, gpt at the margin). The `tested` status now rests on firmer footing; what stays open is human comparison + defeasance competence vs strict-NLI labeling. `internal-contrast-only`. Candidate anchor Scivetti CxNLI. `contingent-on: []`. (**theory + empirical**)
- [`findings/conjectures/distributional-saturation-grounding-headroom.md`](findings/conjectures/distributional-saturation-grounding-headroom.md) — status: **tested — gating shape only** (predictions 1–2), promoted `proposed → tested` 2026-06-28 (session 130, cross-session autonomous adversarial review, against the s121 v2 run); **prediction 3 (magnitude) stays explicitly UNTESTED and — per the s130 open-access scout — un-instrumentable on current open resources** (an externally-released graded-image set is owed; in-house build out of charter reach). - [`findings/conjectures/commutative-convention.md`](findings/conjectures/commutative-convention.md) — status: **RETIRED — FALSIFIED (2026-06-16, twentieth session)** by [`result/relational-spontaneous-recency-a`](findings/results/relational-spontaneous-recency-a.md) (Option A): when a term is **reassigned** so only recency disambiguates, both models recover it by its **most-recent binding** at ceiling → **order-sensitive (non-commutative)**. The positive is promoted to [`claim/relational-order-sensitive-reassignment`](findings/claims/relational-order-sensitive-reassignment.md); commutativity is **operationalization-dependent** (the v1/v4 nulls stand as bounded observations where order carried no disambiguating signal or was confounded with position). *Original (proposed, 2026-05-31):* **the project's own ORIGINAL conjecture**, naming the relational pilot's verdict precisely: LLM referential conventions are (so far) **commutative** — recovered from the content-*set*, not the ordered trajectory — the **aggregation (commutative) vs. constitution (non-commutative)** distinction that makes "coordination, not constitution" exact. A deflationary forward bet that the order-invariance persists; the predicted human contrast was sharpened 2026-06-12 against [`base/sources/brennan-clark-1996-conceptual-pacts.md`](base/sources/brennan-clark-1996-conceptual-pacts.md): humans form partner-indexed, historical pacts (anchored), while human *order-sensitivity* — the pole the contrast needs — is untested by that source (it reports frequency-over-recency) and stays an open question. Decisive test = the v2 history-perturbation arm — **first attempt ran 2026-06-12 → INCONCLUSIVE/MIXED** ([`result/relational-history-perturbation-v2`](findings/results/relational-history-perturbation-v2.md)): neither falsified nor strengthened; the test remains open (position/chronology confound identified by the direction-control arm). Generalizes a bounded, under-powered null ([`result/relational-reference-game-v1`](findings/results/relational-reference-game-v1.md)); trajectory measure internal-contrast-only; v1 yardstick **ratified 2026-06-12**. `contingent-on: []`. (**theory session / relational axis**)
- [`findings/conjectures/preference-commitment-generality.md`](findings/conjectures/preference-commitment-generality.md) — status: **tested → NOT CONFIRMED** (2026-06-15); the forward bet that the AANN preference/commitment dissociation is a **general property of divergent-default constructions** was tested on the conative ([`result/conative-preference-commitment-v1`](findings/results/conative-preference-commitment-v1.md), VERDICT INCONCLUSIVE) and the **first generalization attempt failed to reproduce the AANN shape**: the paraphrase double contrast was non-positive in all three models (the bare-*at* lexical cue absorbs the cancel-preference) and the only construction effect was a single model's *commitment-only* shift — the mirror of AANN. The dissociation reads as **AANN-specific so far**; the conceptual "two constructs" point survives, the "general ordering" claim does not. One construction cannot prove AANN-uniqueness — the way/caused-motion near-miss fallback could revisit it. `contingent-on: []`. (**grammatical / empirical track**)

### Findings — essays

- [`findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md`](findings/essays/antonymy-outlier-distributional-shadow.md) — status: **draft** (2026-06-29, session 146); **"The antonymy outlier is the distributional shadow showing through"** (lexical / philosophical track). Original contribution, a **deflationary reading** of the convergent finding that **antonymy is the lexical relation models recover best** — Cao 2025 ("antonymy the outlier… models perform reasonably well", behavioral/human-compared) and Diera & Scherp 2026 ("antonymy easiest", representational) agree from opposite methods. The reading: antonymy is the relation most fully cued by **symmetric contrastive co-occurrence**, so on Harris's form-internal contrast measure it is **maximally Harris-recoverable** ([`essay/two-distributional-hypotheses`](findings/essays/two-distributional-hypotheses.md)) — the relation where the [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md) "beat the distributional shadow" residual is **smallest**, hence the **shadow cast most fully, not beaten**. Sharpest rigor move: the **cross-*method*** convergence does **not screen off** the distributional cause (both probes are downstream of the same training-time co-occurrence), so by the **screening-off** logic of [`essay/cross-level-convergence-ladder`](findings/essays/cross-level-convergence-ladder.md) — *applied* to a cross-method (not cross-level) case, explicitly **not** a claim the ladder makes — the convergence **raises the prior on deflation**, it does not triangulate competence. Handles the antonym/synonym **distributional paradox** by splitting relatum-*production* (easy, frame-cued) from antonym-vs-synonym *discrimination* (hard) — one distributional cause, two readings, which **strengthens** the thesis. Bounded: predicts/consistent-with/raises-prior, **does not** measure the over-and-above residual to zero; **no human comparison of its own** (Cao's gap cited as prior-art at its strength, older/smaller models), **no claim about the project's panel** (that bet is the companion conjecture, blocked). Four revision triggers (headline: a panel relatum probe with a contrastive-frame control showing antonymy competence *surviving* = clean falsifier); **trigger (d) fired twice, both confirming — s148 (J&K 1991, adjectives) and s149 (Cao et al. 2025 \*SEM, cross-PoS/cross-relation on COCA), extending the contrastive-frame premise to nouns/verbs/adverbs on its co-occurrence-*strength* leg, with the parallel-frame *mechanism* for nouns left inferential.** `depends-on` [`source/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge`](base/sources/cao-2025-semantic-relation-knowledge.md) + [`source/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy`](base/sources/cao-2025-distinctive-cooccurrence-antonymy.md) + [`source/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations`](base/sources/diera-2026-encode-semantic-relations.md) + [`source/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence`](base/sources/justeson-katz-1991-antonym-cooccurrence.md) + [`source/harris-1954-distributional-structure`](base/sources/harris-1954-distributional-structure.md) + [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md) + [`concept/inferential-meaning`](base/concepts/inferential-meaning.md) + [`theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum`](findings/theory/lexicon-grammar-continuum.md) + [`essay/two-distributional-hypotheses`](findings/essays/two-distributional-hypotheses.md) + [`essay/cross-level-convergence-ladder`](findings/essays/cross-level-convergence-ladder.md); `supports` [`conjecture/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation`](findings/conjectures/lexical-relation-shadow-saturation.md); `contingent-on: []`. - [`findings/essays/nothing-to-cancel.md`](findings/essays/nothing-to-cancel.md) — status: **revised** (created s136; revised s138, and again reacting to the s141 within-verbal confirm — recorded s142: the case-(i) precondition is now met on a **clean within-verbal** cancel arm, M2 discharged, suppression partial/verb-uneven, no human comparison); **"Nothing to cancel"** (philosophical / constructional track). Original contribution, a **two-failure-modes distinction on the cancel side**: a "cancel" test can be hard either because **(i)** the model *holds* the default as a (near-)entailment but **fails to suppress it** (genuine defeasance — the conjecture's actual claim) or because **(ii)** the model *never held* the default as an entailment (it was only an **implicature** — *nothing to cancel*, an **unbuildable** test), and conflating them corrupts the [`conjecture/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md) monotonicity reading. The s135 B2 NO-GO is case (ii), caught by the gate before any asymmetry was read; the conative cancel arm worked because contact *is* a held entailment (case (i)). A fair cancel test needs a **held entailment as its target** — exactly what the B2 default-at-ceiling gate certifies. Bounded **positive** (kept thin): the panel *labels* the "only once" implicature neutral under strict NLI, as a strict-NLI annotator should — not "understanding" implicature. Second by-product: the recurring cancel-arm trouble is *also a map of which defaults these models hold as entailments* (contact: yes; single-occurrence: no). **Design-agnostic** (names no redesign winner; the redesign decision [`decisions/resolved/monotonicity-cancel-arm-redesign`](decisions/resolved/monotonicity-cancel-arm-redesign.md) was resolved this session and **affirms** the essay's B2-gate precondition); **no human comparison** (both cited results `internal-contrast-only`; the s135 asymmetry was never read). Distinct from [`essay/add-cancel-separability`](findings/essays/add-cancel-separability.md) (the mirror-image precondition on the **add** side — control off-ceiling vs cancel default on-ceiling), [`essay/predictive-objective-favors-accumulation`](findings/essays/predictive-objective-favors-accumulation.md) (downstream: the asymmetry's *direction*), [`essay/inference-default-coincidence`](findings/essays/inference-default-coincidence.md) (add-side coincidence). `refines` [`conjecture/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md); `depends-on` [`result/monotonicity-generalization-b2-nogo-v1`](findings/results/monotonicity-generalization-b2-nogo-v1.md) + [`result/conative-cancel-direction-v2`](findings/results/conative-cancel-direction-v2.md) + [`concept/coercion`](base/concepts/coercion.md) + [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md); `contingent-on: []`. - [`findings/essays/alignment-names-the-floor.md`](findings/essays/alignment-names-the-floor.md) — status: **draft** (2026-06-28, session 136); **"Alignment names the floor"** (relational / philosophical track). - [`findings/essays/add-cancel-separability.md`](findings/essays/add-cancel-separability.md) — status: **revised** (2026-06-28; draft s132, revised s133 when its trigger (a) fired — see below); **"Are the two poles separable?"** (philosophical / constructional track). Original contribution, a **premise-level caution**: the add-easy/cancel-hard **monotonicity** framing ([`conjecture/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md)) presupposes that the "added" entailment and the "lexical default" are **cleanly separable** — but in a **distributional** system that joint is not pre-given: when a control verb already co-occurs with the would-be-added entailment the add arm has no headroom (the default-coincidence trap), and a "default to be cancelled" is itself just a strong distributional prior, not a different *kind* of content. So the add/cancel dichotomy is an **operational achievement of careful item construction**, with the recurring difficulty of building a headroom-bearing add arm as its **empirical shadow**. Frames as a **sharpening, not a refutation**: a clean asymmetry result depends on first earning a clean per-pair separation. No human comparison; the both-poles-as-priors claim is labeled interpretation. Distinct from [`essay/predictive-objective-favors-accumulation`](findings/essays/predictive-objective-favors-accumulation.md) (assumes the asymmetry, reads its *direction*), [`essay/inference-default-coincidence`](findings/essays/inference-default-coincidence.md) (the AANN worked instance — this generalizes it to the framing), and [`essay/gradient-from-overlap`](findings/essays/gradient-from-overlap.md) (lexical representation axis). **Revised s133:** the essay's pre-declared trigger (a) FIRED — [`result/addarm-headroom-calibration-v1`](findings/results/addarm-headroom-calibration-v1.md) demonstrated clean add-arm headroom on two new construction pairs, so the worry is now scoped to pairs where separability has NOT been demonstrated; the **core thesis is vindicated** (separability had to be *earned* by verb selection, and was earnable; the trap is confirmed real but verb-specific). Trigger (b) did NOT fire (add arms did not collapse). `refines` [`conjecture/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry`](findings/conjectures/constructional-monotonicity-asymmetry.md) + [`result/addarm-headroom-calibration-v1`](findings/results/addarm-headroom-calibration-v1.md); `depends-on` [`concept/coercion`](base/concepts/coercion.md), [`concept/distributional-meaning`](base/concepts/distributional-meaning.md), and the answer-key / implicit-cue results. (created 2026-06-28; **philosophical track**)
